APPENDIXD:
THREE LANE, THREE BOX GIRDER BRIDGE DESIGN RESULTS

D.I Design Results for Three-Lane, Three-Box Girder Bridge D.1.1 Design Code:
Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code of 2000, CAN/CSA-S6-00.

D.1.2 Roadway:
Class A, 4-lane undivided urban roadway

D.1.3 Design Approach:
Longitudinal moments and shear forces are calculated using the "simplified method of analysis" for both dead and live loads, in accordance with clauses 5.6.1 and 5.7.1 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code. The "empirical method of analysis" will be used for the deck slab in accordance with clauses 8.18.4 and 8.15.5 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24). See, three-lane, three-box girder, Figure 4.11 for Cross-Section and Figure 4.12 for Girder Elevation.

D.2 Material Properties D.2.1 Steel:
G40.21 grade 350A and 350AT (Atmospheric resistant, notch-tough) Modulus of elasticity: Es = 200,000 Mpa, Shear Modulus: Gs = 77,000 Mpa Minimum specified yield stress: Fy = 350 Mpa (structural steel) fy = 400 Mpa (reinforcing bars). The main density: 7800 kg I m 3 ; material density: 77 kN 1m3

D.2.2 Concrete:
28-day strength: (
=

30 Mpa

Mass density: y = 2400 kg I m 3 Modulus of elasticity, Clause 8.4.1.7 of CHBDC (24): Ec = 24 800 Mpa.

D-l

D.2.3 Design Lanes:

Deck width, We = 11.25 m. Number of design lanes, n=3. Design lane width: We = We / n = 11.25/3 = 3.75 m, clause 3.8.2 ofCHBDC (24). Modification factor for multi-lane loading: n=3, RL = 0.8, clause 3.8.4.2 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
D.2.4 Dynamic Load Allowance:

Truck load, 3 axles or more (ULS, SLS and FLS): DLA = 0.25, clause 3.8.4.5 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
D.2.S Vibrations and Serviceability:

The bridge is designed for occasional pedestrian use.

D.3 Cross Section Design:

For three-lane, three-box girder bridge section: A 1600 mm web depth was selected for the bridge, resulting in a span-to-depth ratio of 30. The roadway deck features a 225 mm concrete slab topped by a 90 mm asphalt wearing surface.
D.3.t Requirements of the "Simplified Method of Analysis" for Live Load

Clause 5.7.1.1 ofthe CHBDC (24) specifies few limitations for the use of simplified design method of analysis as follows: a) The bridge width is constant. b) Support conditions corresponds to line supports. c) Skew limits are satisfied (the bridge is unskewed).

D-2

d) Horizontal curvature limits are satisfied (The bridge is straight). e) The length of the slab taper near free edges does not exceed 2.5 m.
t) There are at least 3 equally spaced longitudinal girders of equal flexural rigidity.

g) Slab overhang: 1190 mm < 60% of spacing between two outermost webs = 0.60 x 2350 = 1410 mm. 1190 mm < 1800 mm. h) The provisions A5.1(a) ofCHBDC (24) apply. i) Each spine (or box) has only 2 webs, .and the conditions of clause 10.12.5.1 of CHBDC (24) apply.
D.3.2 Requirements of the "Empirical Design Method" of Deck Slabs

Clause 8.18.4.1 of the CHBDC (24) specifies limitations for the use of the simplified design method for deck slabs as follows: a) The deck slab is composite with the supporting, parallel girders. b) Maximum girder web spacing: 2360 mm < 18 x Slab thickness = 18 x 225 c) The maximum girder web spacing: 2360 mm < 4000 mm d) The requirements of section 10 of CHBDC (24) regarding longitudinal reinforcement apply e) The "empirical design method" requires a maximum intermediate cross frame spacing of8 m as stated in clause 8.18.5 ofCHBDC (24).

D.6 Slab Reinforcement

Since the cross-frame spacing does not exceed 8 m, the "empirical design method", clause 8.18.4 ofCHBDC (24) is used for the slab reinforcement.

D.6.1 Minimum Concrete Cover

Table 8.11.2.2 of the CHBDC (24) provides information about the minimum concrete cover. For an environmental exposure including de-icing chemicals, cast-in place concrete: Rebar diameter, 15M: 16.0 mm. Top rebars, minimum cover = 70 mm.

D-8

Top longitudinal rebar depth = 70 + 16 + 16/2 = 94 mm. Minimum cover for bottom rebars (soffit, slab thickness<300 mm)=50mm Bottom transverse rebar depth (for calculating effective depth of concrete, d, lower reinforcing assembly, clause 8.18.4.2.(a) of CHBDC (24), = 225 - 50 - 16 / 2 = 167 mm.

D.6.2 Empirical Slab Design Method Requirements

Slab thickness: 225 mm> 175 mm, clause 8.18.2 ofCHBDC (24). Reinforcement ratio, p 2 0.003, clause 8.18.4.2 (a) ofCHBDC (24). Rebar spacing ~ 300 mm, clause 8.18.4.2 (e) ofCHBDC (24).

D.6.3 Longitudinal Reinforcement and Transverse Reinforcement

Number of rebars, top and bottom, within effective width = Effective width / Rebar spacing = 4270 / 300 = 14.

+ Abottom = 14 (200) + 14 (200) = 5600 mm2

D.6.5 Transverse Slab Moments in the Cantilever Overhang

Since the empirical design method is used for the transverse reinforcement, only the transverse moments due to loads on the overhang need be checked, clause 8.18.1 of CHBDC (24). Moments due to wheel loads on sidewalk are calculated using clauses 3.8.4.4 and 5.7.1.6.1 of CHBDC (24). Design assumptions for this case are based on the 225 mm structural slab only, conservatively ignoring the stiffness contributions of the sidewalk and barrier.

D.7 Section Properties
Four different sets of section properties are calculated, depending on the construction stage and type of loading: 1. 2. 3. Before composite action bare steel girder only After composite action, 1 x n: live loads (Sn) After composite action, 3 x n : dead loads applied after composite action, to account for creep and shrinkage an accordance with Clause 10.11.3 (S3n) 4. After composite action, negative moment regions: steel girder and the reinforcing bars only (S')

D.7.1 Steel- Concrete modular ratio
Short-term loads: n = Es I Ee = 200,000 I 24,800 = 8.06 Long-term loads (including creep and shrinkage):

D-12

3n = 3 x 8.06 = 24.2

D.7.2 Stiffness Analysis

Negative bending moments at the supports are computed assuming full structural continuity, that is, using uncracked composite sections. Therefore, the analysis is based on fully composite sections using a modular ratio of 1 x n in both positive and negative moment regions.

D.9 Simplified Method of Analysis - Live Load Amplification Factors
Live load amplification factors (Fm and Fv) enable the calculation of longitudinal moments and shear forces using a simple, one-dimensional, line element mode, provided the requirements the "Simplified Method of Analysis" ,given in clause 5.7.1 ofCHBDC (24), are satisfied.

D.I0.4 Shear Resistance

The shear resistance is calculated in accordance with clauses 10.10.5.1 and 10.12.3 of CHBDC (24). In the following example, the shear resistance of the trapezoidal box girder, Vr, is taken equal to the sum of the resistances of each web, multiplied by cose , where e is the angle of inclination of the web plate with respect to vertical.

The stiffened box girder has been divided longitudinally into different zones, in addition to the anchor panel zone located at the abutments, to determine shear resistance. Each zone has a different web stiffener spacing. The resisting shear stress of a stiffened web panel consists of two components, Fs = Fer + Ft. where Fer is the shear buckling stress, and Ft is the tension field component.

Web inclination angle: e = 14.0° , cose = 0.970 Factored shear force applied on the girder: Vf= 639 kN (ULS after composite action) Web height, h = 1600/ cose = 1600/0.97 = 1649 mm Web slenderness ratio, h/w = 1649/10 = 164.9
3150/ ,jFy = 168 > 164.9 Longitudinal stiffeners are not required (clause 10.10.4.2).

D.13 Control of Cracking, SLS

The requirements for control of cracking of the concrete slab are given in clause 8.12 of CHBDC (24). However, since the slab reinforcement is designed in accordance with the empirical design method, these requirements are waived, clause 8.18.1 of CHBDC (24).

D.14 Superstructure Vibrations, SLS

The maximum deflection due to a single truck, including dynamic allowance, should not exceed the limit given in CHBDC (24), Figure 3.4.4. The deflection limit depends on the fundamental frequency of the bridge and the anticipated pedestrian use. Because the two spans are equal, a simplified method will be used to estimate the fundamental frequency.

Average moment of inertia of an exterior girder (composite, 1x n): 1= 1.08 Ell mm4

D.tS Fatigue
Fatigue stress ranges are based on FLS moments computed using the live load of a single truck, clause 5.7.1.2.2 ofCHBDC (24). Load induced fatigue may be disregarded at locations where the compressive stress due to permanent loads is at least twice the maximum tensile stress due to the live loads, clause 10.17.2.1 of CHBDC (24). The following design requirement must be satisfied.

0.52 fsr < Fsr (Clause 10.17.2.2 ofCHBDC (24)).

where fsr is the calculated stress range due to the passage of a CL-W truck and Fsr is the fatigue stress range resistance of a member or a detail.

APPENDIXE:
THREE LANE, FOUR BOX GIRDER BRIDGE DESIGN RESULTS

E.1 Design Results for Three-Lane, Four-Box Girder Bridge E.1.1 Design Code:

Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code of 2000, CAN/CSA-S6-00.
E.1.2 Roadway:

Class A, 4-lane undivided urban roadway
E.1.3 Design Approach:

Longitudinal moments and shear forces are calculated using the "simplified method of analysis" for both dead and live loads, in accordance with clauses 5.6.1 and 5.7.1 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code. The "empirical method of analysis" will be used for the deck slab in accordance with Clauses 8.18.4 and 8.15.5 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24). See, three-lane four-box girder, Figure 4.14 for Cross-Section and Figure 4.15 for Girder Elevation.

E.2 Material Properties E.2.1 Steel:

G40.21 grade 350A and 350AT (Atmospheric resistant, notch-tough) Modulus of elasticity: Es = 200,000 Mpa, Shear Modulus: Gs = 77,000 Mpa Minimum specified yield stress: Fy = 350 Mpa (structural steel) fy = 400 Mpa (reinforcing bars). The main density: 7800 kg I m 3 ; material density: 77 kN 1m3
E.2.2 Concrete:

28-day strength: (

=

30 Mpa

Mass density: y = 2400 kg I m 3 Modulus of elasticity, clause 8.4.1. 7 of CHBDC (24): Ec = 24 800 Mpa.

E-l

E.2.3 Design Lanes:

Deck width, We = 11.25 m Number of design lanes, n=3 Design lane width: We = We 1 n = 11.25/3 = 3.75 m ,clause 3.8.2 ofCHBDC (24) Modification factor for multi-lane loading: n=3, RL = 0.8, clause 3.8.4.2 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
E.2.4 Dynamic Load Allowance:

Truck load, 3 axles or more (ULS, SLS and FLS): DLA = 0.25, clause 3.8.4.5 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
E.2.5 Vibrations and Serviceability:

The bridge is designed for occasional pedestrian use.

E.3 Cross Section Design:

For three-lane, four-box girder bridge section: A 1600 mm web depth was selected for the bridge, resulting in a span-to-depth ratio of 30. The roadway deck features a 225 mm concrete slab topped by a 90 mm asphalt wearing surface.
E.3.1 Requirements of the "Simplified Method of Analysis" for Live Load

Clause 5.7.1.1 of the CHBDC (24) specifies few limitations for the use of simplified design method of analysis as follows: a) The bridge width is constant b) Support conditions corresponds to line supports c) Skew limits are satisfied (the bridge is unskewed)

E-2

d) Horizontal curvature limits are satisfied (The bridge is straight) e) The length ofthe slab taper near free edges does not exceed 2.5 m

f) There are at least 3 equally spaced longitudinal girders of equal flexural rigidity
g) Slab overhang: 900 mm < 60% of spacing between two outermost webs = 0.60 x 1737.5 = 1042.5 mm 900 mm < 1800 mm h) The provisions A5.1(a) ofCHBDC (24) apply. i) Each spine (or box) has only 2 webs, and the conditions of clause 10.12.5.1 of CHBDC (24) apply. E.3.2 Requirements of the "Empirical Design Method" of Deck Slabs Clause 8.18.4.1 of the CHBDC (24) specifies limitations for the use of the simplified design method for deck slabs as follows: a) The deck slab is composite with the supporting, parallel girders b) Maximum girder web spacing: 1800 mm < 18 x Slab thickness = 18 x 225 = 4050 mm c) The maximum girder web spacing: 1800 mm < 4000 mm d) The requirements of section 10 of CHBDC (24) regarding longitudinal reinforcement apply. e) The "empirical design method" requires a maximum intermediate cross frame spacing of8 m as stated in clause 8.18.5 ofCHBDC (24).

E-3

E.3.3 Requirements for Multiple Box Girders

E.S.2 Bottom Flange
The effective bottom flange width of box girders is calculated according to clause 10.12 .2, using lengths indicated in CHBDC (24), Fig.A5.1 (a). Bottom Flange width = 938 mm < 38,400/5 = 7680 mm The full range is effective.

E.6 Slab Reinforcement
Since the cross-frame spacing does not exceed 8 m, the "empirical design method" clause 8.18.4 of CHBDC (24) is used for the slab reinforcement.

E.6.1 Minimum Concrete Cover
Table 8.11.2.2 of the CHBDC (24) provides information about the minimum concrete cover. For an environmental exposure including de-icing chemicals, cast-in place concrete: Rebar diameter, 15M: 16.0 mm Top rebars, minimum cover = 70 mm

E-8

Top longitudinal rebar depth = 70 + 16 + 16/2 = 94 mm Minimum cover for bottom rebars (soffit, slab thickness<300 mm)=50mm Bottom transverse rebar depth (for calculating effective depth of concrete, d, lower reinforcing assembly, Clause 8. 18.4.2.(a) ofCHBDC (24), = 225 - 50 -16/2 = 167 mm

E.6.2 Empirical Slab Design Method Requirements Slab thickness: 225 mm> 175 mm, Clause 8.18.2 of CHBDC (24). Reinforcement ratio, p ~ 0.003, Clause 8.18.4.2 (a) ofCHBDC (24). Rebar spacing ~ 300 mm, Clause 8.18.4.2 (e) ofCHBDC (24).

E.6.S Transverse Slab Moments in the Cantilever Overhang
Since the empirical design method is used for the transverse reinforcement, only the transverse moments due to loads on the overhang need be checked clause 8.18.1 of CHBDC (24). Moments due to wheel loads on sidewalk are calculated using clauses 3.8.4.4 and 5.7.1.6.1 of CHBDC (24). Design assumptions for this case are based on the 225 mm structural slab only, conservatively ignoring the stiffness contributions of the sidewalk and barrier.

E.7 Section Properties
Four different sets of section properties are calculated, depending on the construction stage and type of loading: 1. 2. 3. Before composite action bare steel girder only After composite action, 1 x n: live loads (Sn ) After composite action, 3 x n : dead loads applied after composite action, to account for creep and shrinkage an accordance with clause 10.11.3 (S3n) 4. After composite action, negative moment regions: steel girder and the reinforcing bars only (S')

E.7.1 Steel- Concrete Modular Ratio
Short-term loads: n = Es I Ee = 200,000 I 24,800 = 8.06 Long-term loads (including creep and shrinkage):

E-12

3n = 3 x 8.06 = 24.2

E.7.2 Stiffness analysis

Negative bending moments at the supports are computed assuming full structural continuity, that is, using uncracked composite sections. Therefore, the analysis is based on fully composite sections using a modular ratio of 1 x n in both positive and negative moment reglOns.

E.9 Simplified Method of Analysis - Live Load Amplification Factors
Live load amplification factors (Fm and Fv) enable the calculation of longitudinal moments and shear forces using a simple, one-dimensional, line element mode, provided the requirements the "Simplified Method of Analysis", given in clause 5.7.1 ofCHBDC (24), are satisfied.

E.I0.4 Shear Resistance The shear resistance is calculated in accordance with clauses 10.10.5.1 and 10.12.3 of CHBDC (24). In the following example, the shear resistance of the trapezoidal box girder, Vr, is taken equal to the sum of the resistances of each web, multiplied by cosS , where S is the angle of inclination of the web plate with respect to vertical.

The stiffened box girder has been divided longitudinally into different zones, in addition to the anchor panel zone located at the abutments, to determine shear resistance. Each zone has a different web stiffener spacing. The resisting shear stress of a stiffened web panel consists of two components, Fs = Fer + Fh where Fer is the shear buckling stress, and Ft is the tension field component.

Web inclination angle: S = 14.0° , cosS = 0.970 Factored shear force applied on the girder: Vf= 477.63 kN (ULS after composite action) Web height, h = 1600/ cosS = 1600/0.97 = 1649 mm Web slenderness ratio, hlw = 1649 / 10 = 164.9 3150/ -VFy = 168 > 164.9 Longitudinal stiffeners are not required (Clause 10.10.4.2). Web area: Aw = 2hw = 2 x 1649 x 10 = 32,980 mm2

E.13 Control of Cracking, SLS

The requirements for control of cracking of the concrete slab are given in clause 8.12 of CHBDC (24). However, since the slab reinforcement is designed in accordance with the empirical design method, these requirements are waived, clause 8.18.1 ofCHBDC (24).

E.14 Superstructure Vibrations, SLS

The maximum deflection due to a single truck, including dynamic allowance, should not exceed the limit given in CHBDC (24), Figure 3.4.4. The deflection limit depends on the fundamental frequency of the bridge and the anticipated pedestrian use. Because the two spans are equal, a simplified method will be used to estimate the fundamental frequency.

Average moment of inertia of an exterior girder (composite, Ix n): 1= 0.84 Ell mm4

E.lS Fatigue
Fatigue stress ranges are based on FLS moments computed using the live load of a single truck, clause 5.7.1.2.2 ofCHBDC (24). Load induced fatigue may be disregarded at locations where the compressive stress due to permanent loads is at least twice the maximum tensile stress due to the live loads, clause 10.17.2.1 of CHBDC (24). The following design requirement must be satisfied.

0.52 fSf < FSf (Clause 10.17.2.2 ofCHBDC (24)).

Where fSf is the calculated stress range due to the passage of a CL-W truck and FSf is the fatigue stress range resistance of a member or a detail.

E.lS.l Detail Categories
Top flange: Category C (stud-type shear connectors), clause 10.17.2.4 of CHBDC (24). Example 13 Fatigue life constant, y = 144 X 1010 (Table 10.17.2.3a) Constant amplitude threshold stress range, Fsrt = 69 MPa Bottom Flange: Category C1 (near transverse stiffener-to-web welds), Example 6
y = 144 X 1010

Fsrt = 83 MPa

APPENDIXF:
THREE-LANE, FIVE-BOX GIRDER BRIDGE DESIGN RESULTS

F.l Design Procedure for Three-Lane, Five-Box Girder Bridge F.1.1 Design Code:

Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code of 2000, CAN/CSA-S6-00.
F.1.2 Roadway:

Class A, 4-lane undivided urban roadway
F.1.3 Design Approach:

Longitudinal moments and shear forces are calculated using the "simplified method of analysis" for both dead and live loads, in accordance with clauses 5.6.1 and 5.7.1 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code. The "empirical method of analysis" will be used for the deck slab in accordance with Clauses 8.18.4 and 8.15.5 of the Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24). See, four-lane, five-box girder, Figure 4.17 for Cross-Section and Figure 4.18 for Girder Elevation.

F.2 Material Properties F.2.1 Steel:

G40.21 grade 350A and 350AT (Atmospheric resistant, notch-tough) Modulus of elasticity: Es = 200,000 Mpa, Shear Modulus: Gs = 77,000 MPa Minimum specified yield stress: Fy = 350 Mpa (structural steel) fy = 400 MPa (reinforcing bars). The main density: 7800 kg I m3 ; material density: 77 kN 1m3
F.2.2 Concrete:

28-day strength: (

=

30 MPa

Mass density: y = 2400 kg I m 3 Modulus of elasticity, clause 8.4.1.7 ofCHBDC (24): Ec = 24800 MPa.

F-l

F.2.3 Design Lanes:

Deck width, We = 11.25 m Number of design lanes, n=3 Design lane width: We = We / n = 11.25/3 = 3.75 m, clause 3.8.2 ofCHBDC (24) Modification factor for multi-lane loading: n=3, RL = 0.8, clause 3.8.4.2 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
F.2.4 Dynamic Load Allowance:

Truck load, 3 axles or more (ULS, SLS and FLS): DLA = 0.25, clause 3.8.4.5 of Canadian Highway Bridge Design Code (24).
F.2.5 Vibrations and Serviceability:

The bridge is designed for occasional pedestrian use.

F.3 Cross Section Design:

For three-lane, five-box girder bridge section: A 1600 mm web depth was selected for the bridge, resulting in a span-to-depth ratio of 30. The roadway deck features a 225 mm concrete slab topped by a 90 mm asphalt wearing surface.
F.3.1 Requirements of the "Simplified Method of Analysis" for Live Load

Clause 5.7.1.1 of the CHBDC (24) specifies few limitations for the use of simplified design method of analysis as follows: a) The bridge width is constant b) Support conditions corresponds to line supports c) Skew limits are satisfied (the bridge is unskewed)

F-2

d) Horizontal curvature limits are satisfied (The bridge is straight) e) The length of the slab taper near free edges does not exceed 2.5 m
f) There are at least 3 equally spaced longitudinal girders of equal flexural rigidity

g) Slab overhang: 800 mm < 60% of spacing between two outermost webs = 0.60 x 1380= 828mm 800mm < 1800mm h) The provisions A5.1(a) ofCHBDC (24) apply. i) Each spine (or box) has only 2 webs, and the conditions of clause 10.12.5.1 of CHBDC (24) apply. F.3.2 Requirements of the "Empirical Design Method" of Deck Slabs Clause 8.18.4.1 of the CHBDC (24) specifies limitations for the use of the simplified design method for deck slabs as follows: a) The deck slab is composite with the supporting, parallel girders b) Maximum girder web spacing: 1412.5 mm < 18 x Slab thickness = 18 x 225 = 4050 mm c) The maximum girder web spacing: 1412.5 mm < 4000 mm d) The requirements of section 10 of CHBDC (24) regarding longitudinal reinforcement apply e) The "empirical design method" requires a maximum intermediate cross frame spacing of8 m as stated in clause 8.18.5 ofCHBDC (24).

F-3

F.3.3 Requirements for Multiple Box Girders
To meet the requirements ofthe definition of multiple box-girder configuration stated in clause 10.12.7.1 ofCHBDC (24), the following limitations are set. a) The centre-to centre flange spacing is constant b) Centre-to-centre flange spacing: 0.80:::; flange spacing between adjacent boxes = 1412.5 flange spacing within boxes 1380

= 1.02:::; 1.20 c) Cantilever slab overhang: 800 mm < 60 % of spacing between top flanges of adjacent boxes = 0.60 x 1412.5 = 847.5mm 800 mm < 1800 mm

F.3.4 Inflexion Points
For the purpose of calculating lengths L, effective slab widths, and live load amplification factors, assumed inflexion points under dead load are given in the following. Positive moment, mid-span : L = 0.8 LI = 0.8 (48 000) = 38 400 mm Negative moment, at pier: L=0.25 (LI + Lz) = 0.25 (48 000 + 48 000) = 24 000 mm

F-4

F.4 Loads on Exterior Girder
Load factors and load combinations will follow clause 3.5.1 of the CHBDC (24) as indicated in the following sub sections.

F.4.3 Assumed Construction Live Loads on Non-Composite Section
The construction loads and load distribution assumed in the design must be observed during construction, unless measures are taken to ensure structural adequacy. Clause 3.16.3 ofCHBDC (24), construction live load factor = 0.85 x 1.7 = 1.45 Bidwell finishing machine wheel load, on cantilever brackets: 24.7 kN/m x 1.45 =35.81 kN/m. Walkway live load, on cantilever brackets (2.4 kPa) : 1.8 kN/m x 1.45 = 2.61 kN/m

F.6 Slab Reinforcement
Since the cross-frame spacing does not exceed 8 m, the "empirical design method", clause 8.18.4 ofCHBDC (24), is used for the slab reinforcement.

F.6.1 Minimum Concrete Cover
Table 8.11.2.2 of the CHBDC (24) provides information about the minimum concrete cover. For an environmental exposure including de-icing chemicals, cast-in place concrete: Rebar diameter, 15M: 16.0 mm Top rebars, minimum cover = 70 mm

F-8

Top longitudinal rebar depth = 70 + 16 + 16 / 2 = 94 mm Minimum cover for bottom rebars (soffit, slab thickness<300 mm)=50mm Bottom transverse rebar depth (for calculating effective depth of concrete, d, lower reinforcing assembly, Clause 8.18.4.2.(a) of CHBDC (24), = 225 - 50 - 16 / 2 = 167 mm

F.6.2 Empirical Slab Design Method Requirements Slab thickness: 225 mm> 175 mm, Clause 8.18.2 ofCHBDC (24). Reinforcement ratio, p ~ 0.003, Clause 8. 18.4.2(a) ofCHBDC (24). Rebar spacing ~ 300 mm, Clause 8.18.4.2 (e) ofCHBDC (24).

F.6.5 Transverse Slab Moments in the Cantilever Overhang

Since the empirical design method is used for the transverse reinforcement, only the transverse moments due to loads on the overhang need be checked, clause 8.18.1 of CHBDC (24). Moments due to wheel loads on sidewalk are calculated using clauses 3.8.4.4 and 5.7.1.6.1 of CHBDC (24). Design assumptions for this case are based on the 225 mm structural slab only, conservatively ignoring the stiffness contributions of the sidewalk and barrier.

Maximum moment occurs at x = y = 0, C / Se = 0.05 /0.35 = 0.142, A:::: 0.53 Figure 5.7.1.6.1 Taking 70% ofthe truck load, P = 175/2 = 87.5 kN (Clause 3.8.4.4) My = 2 P A / 1t = [2 (0.7 x 87.5) 0.53] /1t = 20.67 kNm / m Total factored moment including wheel loads, slab, barrier and sidewalk: Mf= 1.7 x 1.4 x 20.67 + 1.2 x 7.28 = 57.93 kN / m where 1 + DLA = 1.4 for a single truck axle. Tandem axles 2 + 3 (P = 62.5 kN) do not govern in this case.

F.7 Section Properties
Four different sets of section properties are calculated, depending on the construction stage and type of loading: 1. 2. 3. Before composite action bare steel girder only After composite action, 1 x n: live loads (Sn ) After composite action, 3 x n : dead loads applied after composite action, to account for creep and shrinkage an accordance with clause 10.11.3 (S3n) 4. After composite action, negative moment regions: steel girder and the reinforcing bars only (S')

F.7.2 Stiffness Analysis

Negative bending moments at the supports are computed assuming full structural continuity, that is, using uncracked composite sections. Therefore, the analysis is based on fully composite sections using a modular ratio of 1 x n in both positive and negative moment regions.

F.9 Simplified Method of Analysis - Live Load Amplification Factors
Live load amplification factors (Fm and Fv) enable the calculation of longitudinal moments and shear forces using a simple, one-dimensional, line element mode, provided the requirements the "Simplified Method of Analysis", given in clause 5.7.1 ofCHBDC (24), are satisfied.

In positive moment regions, the composite moment resistance is calculated using a fully plastic stress distribution clauses 10.11. 6.2 and 10.12.5.1 of CHBDC (24), with the portion of the web in compression limited to a depth of 850 w / ...JFy. Where section properties change at a reference point, the least properties are assumed.

F.I0.4 Shear Resistance

The shear resistance is calculated in accordance with clauses 10.10.5.1 and 10.12.3 of CHBDC (24). In the following example, the shear resistance of the trapezoidal box girder, Vr, is taken equal to the sum of the resistances of each web, multiplied by cose, where e is the angle of inclination of the web plate with respect to vertical.

The stiffened box girder has been divided longitudinally into different zones, in addition to the anchor panel zone located at the abutments, to determine shear resistance. Each zone has a different web stiffener spacing. The resisting shear stress of a stiffened web panel consists of two components, Fs = Fer + Ft , where Fer is the shear buckling stress, and Ft is the tension field component.

Web inclination angle: e = 14.0° , cose = 0.970 Factored shear force applied on the girder: Vf= 390.11 kN (ULS after composite action) Web height, h = 1600 / cose = 1600 / 0.97 = 1649 mm Web slenderness ratio, h/w = 1649/10 = 164.9 3150 / ...JFy = 168 > 164.9 Longitudinal stiffeners are not required (Clause 10.10.4.2). Web area: Aw = 2hw = 2 x 1649 x 10 = 32,980 mm2

F-39

Try unstiffened web , a / h = 00 Shear buckling coefficient: kv = 5.34 Fer= 180,000 kv / (h/wi = 180,000 x 5.34/164.92 = 35.35 Mpa Ft = 0 Shear stress: Fs = Fer = 35.35 MPa Girder Shear resistance : Vr =~s Aw Fs cosS = 0.95 x 32,980 x 35.35 x cos(14.0) = 1074.60 kN > 390.11 kN

F.12 Shear Resistance of Anchor Panels F.12.1 Anchor Panel Zone, Near Abutments
It is usually impractical to provide effective means of anchoring the tension field. In an end

panel. Therefore, the end panels are proportioned to serve as anchor panels such that tension fields can be developed in the interior panels. The shear resistance of end panels is calculated by setting Ft = 0, clause 10.10.5.1 ofCHBDC (24).

F.13 Control of Cracking, SLS
The requirements for control of cracking of the concrete slab are given in clause 8.12 of CHBDC (24). However, since the slab reinforcement is designed in accordance with the empirical design method, these requirements are waived, clause 8.18.1 of CHBDC (24).

F.14 Superstructure Vibrations, SLS
The maximum deflection due to a single truck, including dynamic allowance, should not exceed the limit given in CHBDC (24), Figure 3.4.4. The deflection limit depends on the fundamental frequency of the bridge and the anticipated pedestrian use. Because the two spans are equal, a simplified method will be used to estimate the fundamental frequency.

Average moment of inertia of an exterior girder (composite, Ix n):

1= 0.72 Ell mm4

F.lS Fatigue Fatigue stress ranges are based on FLS moments computed using the live load of a single truck clause 5.7.1.2.2 of CHBDC (24). Load induced fatigue may be disregarded at locations where the compressive stress due to permanent loads is at least twice the maximum tensile stress due to the live loads, clause 10.17.2.1 of CHBDC (24). The following design requirement must be satisfied.

0.52 fsr < Fsr (Clause 10.17.2.2 ofCHBDC (24».

where fsr is the calculated stress range due to the passage of a CL-W truck and Fsr is the fatigue stress range resistance of a member or a detail.

F.IS.I Detail Categories Top flange: Category C (stud-type shear connectors), clause 10.17.2.4 ofCHBDC (24). Reinforcing Bars
Fatigue requirements do not apply to transverse reinforcing bars designed according to the Empirical Design Method (8.18.4), but fatigue must be considered for longitudinal bars that are part of composite girders (CHBDC Commentary 8.5.3.1). Maximum fatigue stress range for rebars (Clause 8.5.3.1) Straight bars: 125 MPa At anchorages, connections, bends, and welded splices: 65 MPa
